# big-code-pg-arch-001: PostgreSQL Query Execution Pipeline

## Task

Trace the PostgreSQL query execution pipeline from parse to execute. Starting from `exec_simple_query()` in the traffic cop, map how a SQL string flows through the parser (lexer + grammar), semantic analyzer, query rewriter, planner/optimizer, and executor, identifying the data structures that flow between each stage.

## Context

- **Repository**: postgres/postgres (C, ~1.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: src/backend/ — parser, rewrite, optimizer, executor subsystems

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the query pipeline (traffic cop, parser, analyzer, rewriter, planner, executor, node type definitions)
2. Trace the dependency chain from `exec_simple_query()` through each pipeline stage, identifying the data type transformations (RawStmt -> Query -> PlannedStmt -> tuples)
3. Document the two-phase optimization (Path generation via allpaths.c, then Plan creation via createplan.c)
4. Explain the Volcano-style executor dispatch in execProcnode.c

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

## What Was Written

The document traces the complete PostgreSQL simple-query execution pipeline across six narrative sections, each grounded in exact source locations:

### Stage 2 — Parser (`parser/parser.c:42`)
Covers `pg_parse_query()` → `raw_parser()` → `scanner_init()` (re-entrant Flex, `scan.l`) → `base_yyparse()` (LALR(1) Bison, `gram.y`, single-token lookahead filter in `base_yylex()`). Output: `List<RawStmt*>` with `stmt`, `stmt_location`, `stmt_len`.

- **`transformStmt()`** dispatch table across all DML types and the utility-statement fallback. Per-node work: catalog name resolution, range-table building, `Var` annotation.
- `Query` struct field inventory (20+ fields with types and semantics).
- **`QueryRewrite()`**: three-phase sequence — `RewriteQuery()` (DO INSTEAD/DO ALSO rules), `fireRIRrules()` (view expansion, ON SELECT rules, `AcquireRewriteLocks`), `canSetTag` determination.

### Stage 4 — Planner (`planner.c`, `planmain.c`, `allpaths.c`, `createplan.c`)
- `standard_planner()` global state setup and path selection.

Since utility statements\n * aren't allowed within larger statements, this is only allowed at the top\n * of the parse tree, and so we only try it before entering the recursive\n * transformStmt() processing.\n */\nstatic Query *\ntransformOptionalSelectInto(ParseState *pstate, Node *parseTree)\n{\n        if (IsA(parseTree, SelectStmt))\n        {\n                SelectStmt *stmt = (SelectStmt *) parseTree;\n\n                /* If it's a set-operation tree, drill down to leftmost SelectStmt */\n                while (stmt && stmt->op != SETOP_NONE)\n                        stmt = stmt->larg;\n                Assert(stmt && IsA(stmt, SelectStmt) && stmt->larg == NULL);\n\n                if (stmt->intoClause)\n                {\n                        CreateTableAsStmt *ctas = makeNode(CreateTableAsStmt);\n\n                        ctas->query = parseTree;\n                        ctas->into = stmt->intoClause;\n                        ctas->objtype = OBJECT_TABLE;\n                        ctas->is_select_into = true;\n\n                        /*\n                         * Remove the intoClause from the SelectStmt. we can't just run it on everything because\n         * raw_expression_tree_walker() doesn't claim to handle utility\n         * statements.\n         */\n        if (Debug_raw_expression_coverage_test)\n        {\n                switch (nodeTag(parseTree))\n                {\n                        case T_SelectStmt:\n                        case T_InsertStmt:\n                        case T_UpdateStmt:\n                        case T_DeleteStmt:\n                        case T_MergeStmt:\n                                (void) test_raw_expression_coverage(parseTree, NULL);\n                                break;\n                        default:\n                                break;\n                }\n        }\n#endif                                                  /* DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED */\n\n        /*\n         * Caution: when changing the set of statement types that have non-default\n         * processing here, see also stmt_requires_parse_analysis() and\n         * analyze_requires_snapshot().\n         */\n        switch (nodeTag(parseTree))\n        {\n                        /*\n                         * Optimizable statements\n                         */\n                case T_InsertStmt:\n                        result = transformInsertStmt(pstate, (InsertStmt *) parseTree);\n                        break;\n\n                case T_DeleteStmt:\n                        result = transformDeleteStmt(pstate, (DeleteStmt *) parseTree);\n                        break;\n\n                case T_UpdateStmt:\n                        result = transformUpdateStmt(pstate, (UpdateStmt *) parseTree);"

"QueryRewrite(Query *parsetree)\n{\n        int64           input_query_id = parsetree->queryId;\n        List       *querylist;\n        List       *results;\n        ListCell   *l;\n        CmdType         origCmdType;\n        bool            foundOriginalQuery;\n        Query      *lastInstead;\n\n        /*\n         * This function is only applied to top-level original queries\n         */\n        Assert(parsetree->querySource == QSRC_ORIGINAL);\n        Assert(parsetree->canSetTag);\n\n        /*\n         * Step 1\n         *\n         * Apply all non-SELECT rules possibly getting 0 or many queries\n         */\n        querylist = RewriteQuery(parsetree, NIL, 0, 0);\n\n        /*\n         * Step 2\n         *\n         * Apply all the RIR rules on each query\n         *\n         * This is also a handy place to mark each query with the original queryId\n         */\n        results = NIL;\n        foreach(l, querylist)\n        {\n                Query      *query = (Query *) lfirst(l);\n\n                query = fireRIRrules(query, NIL);\n\n                query->queryId = input_query_id;\n\n                results = lappend(results, query);\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Step 3\n         *\n         * Determine which, if any, of the resulting queries is supposed to set\n         * the command-result tag; and update the canSetTag fields accordingly.\n         *\n         * If the original query is still in the list, it sets the command tag.\n         * Otherwise, the last INSTEAD query of the same kind as the original is\n         * allowed to set the tag.  (Note these rules can leave us with no query\n         * setting the tag.  The tcop code has to cope with this by setting up a\n         * default tag based on the original un-rewritten query.)\n         *\n         * The Asserts verify that at most one query in the result list is marked\n         * canSetTag.  If we aren't checking asserts, we can fall out of the loop\n         * as soon as we find the original query.\n         */\n        origCmdType = parsetree->commandType;\n        foundOriginalQuery = false;\n        lastInstead = NULL;\n\n        foreach(l, results)\n        {\n                Query      *query = (Query *) lfirst(l);\n\n                if (query->querySource == QSRC_ORIGINAL)\n                {\n                        Assert(query->canSetTag);\n                        Assert(!foundOriginalQuery);\n                        foundOriginalQuery = true;\n#ifndef USE_ASSERT_CHECKING\n                        break;\n#endif\n                }\n                else\n                {\n                        Assert(!query->canSetTag);\n                        if (query->commandType == origCmdType &&\n                                (query->querySource == QSRC_INSTEAD_RULE ||\n                                 query->querySource == QSRC_QUAL_INSTEAD_RULE))\n                                lastInstead = query;\n                }\n        }"

"PlannedStmt *\nplanner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,\n                ParamListInfo boundParams)\n{\n        PlannedStmt *result;\n\n        if (planner_hook)\n                result = (*planner_hook) (parse, query_string, cursorOptions, boundParams);\n        else\n                result = standard_planner(parse, query_string, cursorOptions, boundParams);\n\n        pgstat_report_plan_id(result->planId, false);\n\n        return result;\n}\n\nPlannedStmt *\nstandard_planner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,\n                                 ParamListInfo boundParams)\n{\n        PlannedStmt *result;\n        PlannerGlobal *glob;\n        double          tuple_fraction;\n        PlannerInfo *root;\n        RelOptInfo *final_rel;\n        Path       *best_path;\n        Plan       *top_plan;\n        ListCell   *lp,\n                           *lr;\n\n        /*\n         * Set up global state for this planner invocation. We\n         * can't do this in a standalone backend, or if the command will try to\n         * modify any data, or if this is a cursor operation, or if GUCs are set\n         * to values that don't permit parallelism, or if parallel-unsafe\n         * functions are present in the query tree.\n         *\n         * (Note that we do allow CREATE TABLE AS, SELECT INTO, and CREATE\n         * MATERIALIZED VIEW to use parallel plans, but this is safe only because\n         * the command is writing into a completely new table which workers won't\n         * be able to see.  If the workers could see the table, the fact that\n         * group locking would cause them to ignore the leader's heavyweight GIN\n         * page locks would make this unsafe.  We'll have to fix that somehow if\n         * we want to allow parallel inserts in general; updates and deletes have\n         * additional problems especially around combo CIDs.)\n         *\n         * For now, we don't try to use parallel mode if we're running inside a\n         * parallel worker. It's not safe to do so if\n         * the query contains anything parallel-unsafe; parallelModeOK will be\n         * false in that case. "* make_one_rel\n *        Finds all possible access paths for executing a query, returning a\n *        single rel that represents the join of all base rels in the query.\n */\nRelOptInfo *\nmake_one_rel(PlannerInfo *root, List *joinlist)\n{\n        RelOptInfo *rel;\n        Index           rti;\n        double          total_pages;\n\n        /* Mark base rels as to whether we care about fast-start plans */\n        set_base_rel_consider_startup(root);\n\n        /*\n         * Compute size estimates and consider_parallel flags for each base rel.\n         */\n        set_base_rel_sizes(root);\n\n        /*\n         * We should now have size estimates for every actual table involved in\n         * the query, and we also know which if any have been deleted from the\n         * query by join removal, pruned by partition pruning, or eliminated by\n         * constraint exclusion.  So we can now compute total_table_pages.\n         *\n         * Note that appendrels are not double-counted here, even though we don't\n         * bother to distinguish RelOptInfos for appendrel parents, because the\n         * parents will have pages = 0.\n         *\n         * XXX if a table is self-joined, we will count it once per appearance,\n         * which perhaps is the wrong thing ... but that's not completely clear,\n         * and detecting self-joins here is difficult, so ignore it for now.\n         */\n        total_pages = 0;\n        for (rti = 1; rti < root->simple_rel_array_size; rti++)\n        {\n                RelOptInfo *brel = root->simple_rel_array[rti];\n\n                /* there may be empty slots corresponding to non-baserel RTEs */\n                if (brel == NULL)\n                        continue;\n\n                Assert(brel->relid == rti); /* sanity check on array */\n\n                if (IS_DUMMY_REL(brel))\n                        continue;\n\n                if (IS_SIMPLE_REL(brel))\n                        total_pages += (double) brel->pages;\n        }\n        root->total_table_pages = total_pages;\n\n        /*\n         * Generate access paths for each base rel.\n         */\n        set_base_rel_pathlists(root);\n\n        /*\n         * Generate access paths for the entire join tree.\n         */\n        rel = make_rel_from_joinlist(root, joinlist);\n\n        /*\n         * The result should join all and only the query's base + outer-join rels.\n         */\n        Assert(bms_equal(rel->relids, root->all_query_rels));\n\n        return rel;\n}\n\n/*\n * set_base_rel_consider_startup\n *        Set the consider_[param_]startup flags for each base-relation entry.\n *\n * For the moment, we only deal with consider_param_startup here; If that logic ever gets more complicated it would probably\n * be better to move it here.\n */\nstatic void\nset_base_rel_consider_startup(PlannerInfo *root)\n{\n        /*\n         * Since parameterized paths can only be used on the inside of a nestloop\n         * join plan, there is usually little value in considering fast-start\n         * plans for them. "/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *\n * execProcnode.c\n *       contains dispatch functions which call the appropriate \"initialize\",\n *       \"get a tuple\", and \"cleanup\" routines for the given node type.\n *       If the node has children, then it will presumably call ExecInitNode,\n *       ExecProcNode, or ExecEndNode on its subnodes and do the appropriate\n *       processing.\n *\n * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group\n * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California\n *\n *\n * IDENTIFICATION\n *        src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c\n *\n *-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n */\n/*\n *       NOTES\n *              This used to be three files.  It is now all combined into\n *              one file so that it is easier to keep the dispatch routines\n *              in sync when new nodes are added.\n *\n *       EXAMPLE\n *              Suppose we want the age of the manager of the shoe department and\n *              the number of employees in that department.  So we have the query:\n *\n *                              select DEPT.no_emps, EMP.age\n *                              from DEPT, EMP\n *                              where EMP.name = DEPT.mgr and\n *                                        DEPT.name = \"shoe\"\n *\n *              Suppose the planner gives us the following plan:\n *\n *                                              Nest Loop (DEPT.mgr = EMP.name)\n *                                              /               \\\n *                                         /             \\\n *                                 Seq Scan             Seq Scan\n *                                      DEPT              EMP\n *                              (name = \"shoe\")\n *\n *              ExecutorStart() is called first.\n *              It calls InitPlan() which calls ExecInitNode() on\n *              the root of the plan -- the nest loop node.\n *\n *        * ExecInitNode() notices that it is looking at a nest loop and\n *              as the code below demonstrates, it calls ExecInitNestLoop().\n *              Eventually this calls ExecInitNode() on the right and left subplans\n *              and so forth until the entire plan is initialized.  The result\n *              of ExecInitNode() is a plan state tree built with the same structure\n *              as the underlying plan tree.\n *\n *        * Then when ExecutorRun() is called, it calls ExecutePlan() which calls\n *              ExecProcNode() repeatedly on the top node of the plan state tree.\n *              Each time this happens, ExecProcNode() will end up calling\n *              ExecNestLoop(), which calls ExecProcNode() on its subplans.\n *              Each of these subplans is a sequential scan so ExecSeqScan() is\n *              called.  The slots returned by ExecSeqScan() may contain\n *              tuples which contain the attributes ExecNestLoop() uses to\n *              form the tuples it returns.\n *\n *        * Eventually ExecSeqScan() stops returning tuples and the nest\n *              loop join ends.  Lastly, ExecutorEnd() calls ExecEndNode() which\n *              calls ExecEndNestLoop() which in turn calls ExecEndNode() on\n *              its subplans which result in ExecEndSeqScan().\n *\n *              This should show how the executor works by having\n *              ExecInitNode(), ExecProcNode() and ExecEndNode() dispatch\n *              their work to the appropriate node support routines which may\n *              in turn call these routines themselves on their subplans.\n */\n#include \"postgres.h\"\n\n#include \"executor/executor.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeAgg.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeAppend.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapAnd.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapHeapscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapIndexscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapOr.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeCtescan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeCustom.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeForeignscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeFunctionscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeGather.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeGatherMerge.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeGroup.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeHash.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeHashjoin.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeIncrementalSort.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeIndexonlyscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeIndexscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeLimit.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeLockRows.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMaterial.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMemoize.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMergeAppend.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMergejoin.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeModifyTable.h\""

"*              ExecutePlan\n *\n *              Processes the query plan until we have retrieved 'numberTuples' tuples,\n *              moving in the specified direction.\n *\n *              Runs to completion if numberTuples is 0\n * ----------------------------------------------------------------\n */\nstatic void\nExecutePlan(QueryDesc *queryDesc,\n                        CmdType operation,\n                        bool sendTuples,\n                        uint64 numberTuples,\n                        ScanDirection direction,\n                        DestReceiver *dest)\n{\n        EState     *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n        PlanState  *planstate = queryDesc->planstate;\n        bool            use_parallel_mode;\n        TupleTableSlot *slot;\n        uint64          current_tuple_count;\n\n        /*\n         * initialize local variables\n         */\n        current_tuple_count = 0;\n\n        /*\n         * Set the direction.\n         */\n        estate->es_direction = direction;\n\n        /*\n         * Set up parallel mode if appropriate.\n         *\n         * Parallel mode only supports complete execution of a plan.  If we've\n         * already partially executed it, or if the caller asks us to exit early,\n         * we must force the plan to run without parallelism.\n         */\n        if (queryDesc->already_executed || numberTuples != 0)\n                use_parallel_mode = false;\n        else\n                use_parallel_mode = queryDesc->plannedstmt->parallelModeNeeded;\n        queryDesc->already_executed = true;\n\n        estate->es_use_parallel_mode = use_parallel_mode;\n        if (use_parallel_mode)\n                EnterParallelMode();\n\n        /*\n         * Loop until we've processed the proper number of tuples from the plan.\n         */\n        for (;;)\n        {\n                /* Reset the per-output-tuple exprcontext */\n                ResetPerTupleExprContext(estate);\n\n                /*\n                 * Execute the plan and obtain a tuple\n                 */\n                slot = ExecProcNode(planstate);\n\n                /*\n                 * if the tuple is null, then we assume there is nothing more to\n                 * process so we just end the loop...\n                 */\n                if (TupIsNull(slot))\n                        break;\n\n                /*\n                 * If we have a junk filter, then project a new tuple with the junk\n                 * removed.\n                 *\n                 * Store this new \"clean\" tuple in the junkfilter's resultSlot.\n                 * (Formerly, we stored it back over the \"dirty\" tuple, which is WRONG\n                 * because that tuple slot has the wrong descriptor.)\n                 */\n                if (estate->es_junkFilter != NULL)\n                        slot = ExecFilterJunk(estate->es_junkFilter, slot);\n\n                /*\n                 * If we are supposed to send the tuple somewhere, do so. (In\n                 * practice, this is probably always the case at this point.)\n                 */\n                if (sendTuples)\n                {\n                        /*\n                         * If we are not able to send the tuple, we assume the destination\n                         * has closed and no more tuples can be sent. If that's the case,\n                         * end the loop.\n                         */\n                        if (!dest->receiveSlot(slot, dest))\n                                break;\n                }\n\n                /*\n                 * Count tuples processed, if this is a SELECT.  (For other operation\n                 * types, the ModifyTable plan node must count the appropriate\n                 * events.)\n                 */\n                if (operation == CMD_SELECT)\n                        (estate->es_processed)++;\n\n                /*\n                 * check our tuple count.. if we've processed the proper number then\n                 * quit, else loop again and process more tuples.  Zero numberTuples\n                 * means no limit.\n                 */\n                current_tuple_count++;\n                if (numberTuples && numberTuples == current_tuple_count)\n                        break;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * If we know we won't need to back up, we can release resources at this\n         * point.\n         */\n        if (!(estate->es_top_eflags & EXEC_FLAG_BACKWARD))\n                ExecShutdownNode(planstate);"

"standard_join_search(PlannerInfo *root, int levels_needed, List *initial_rels)\n{\n        int                     lev;\n        RelOptInfo *rel;\n\n        /*\n         * This function cannot be invoked recursively within any one planning\n         * problem, so join_rel_level[] can't be in use already.\n         */\n        Assert(root->join_rel_level == NULL);\n\n        /*\n         * We employ a simple \"dynamic programming\" algorithm: we first find all\n         * ways to build joins of two jointree items, then all ways to build joins\n         * of three items (from two-item joins and single items), then four-item\n         * joins, and so on until we have considered all ways to join all the\n         * items into one rel.\n         *\n         * root->join_rel_level[j] is a list of all the j-item rels. "ExecProcNodeFirst(PlanState *node)\n{\n        /*\n         * Perform stack depth check during the first execution of the node.  We\n         * only do so the first time round because it turns out to not be cheap on\n         * some common architectures (eg. x86).  This relies on the assumption\n         * that ExecProcNode calls for a given plan node will always be made at\n         * roughly the same stack depth.\n         */\n        check_stack_depth();\n\n        /*\n         * If instrumentation is required, change the wrapper to one that just\n         * does instrumentation.  Otherwise we can dispense with all wrappers and\n         * have ExecProcNode() directly call the relevant function from now on.\n         */\n        if (node->instrument)\n                node->ExecProcNode = ExecProcNodeInstr;\n        else\n                node->ExecProcNode = node->ExecProcNodeReal;\n\n        return node->ExecProcNode(node);\n}\n\n\n/*\n * ExecProcNode wrapper that performs instrumentation calls.  By keeping\n * this a separate function, we avoid overhead in the normal case where\n * no instrumentation is wanted.\n */\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNodeInstr(PlanState *node)\n{\n        TupleTableSlot *result;\n\n        InstrStartNode(node->instrument);\n\n        result = node->ExecProcNodeReal(node);\n\n        InstrStopNode(node->instrument, TupIsNull(result) ? 0.0 : 1.0);\n\n        return result;\n}\n\n\n/* ----------------------------------------------------------------\n *              MultiExecProcNode\n *\n *              Execute a node that doesn't return individual tuples\n *              (it might return a hashtable, bitmap, etc).  Caller should\n *              check it got back the expected kind of Node.\n *\n * This has essentially the same responsibilities as ExecProcNode,\n * but it does not do InstrStartNode/InstrStopNode (mainly because\n * it can't tell how many returned tuples to count).  Each per-node\n * function must provide its own instrumentation support.\n * ----------------------------------------------------------------\n */\nNode *\nMultiExecProcNode(PlanState *node)\n{\n        Node       *result;\n\n        check_stack_depth();\n\n        CHECK_FOR_INTERRUPTS();\n\n        if (node->chgParam != NULL) /* something changed */\n                ExecReScan(node);               /* let ReScan handle this */\n\n        switch (nodeTag(node))\n        {\n                        /*\n                         * Only node types that actually support multiexec will be listed\n                         */\n\n                case T_HashState:\n                        result = MultiExecHash((HashState *) node);\n                        break;\n\n                case T_BitmapIndexScanState:\n                        result = MultiExecBitmapIndexScan((BitmapIndexScanState *) node);\n                        break;"

"ExecutePlan(QueryDesc *queryDesc,\n                        CmdType operation,\n                        bool sendTuples,\n                        uint64 numberTuples,\n                        ScanDirection direction,\n                        DestReceiver *dest)\n{\n        EState     *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n        PlanState  *planstate = queryDesc->planstate;\n        bool            use_parallel_mode;\n        TupleTableSlot *slot;\n        uint64          current_tuple_count;\n\n        /*\n         * initialize local variables\n         */\n        current_tuple_count = 0;\n\n        /*\n         * Set the direction.\n         */\n        estate->es_direction = direction;\n\n        /*\n         * Set up parallel mode if appropriate.\n         *\n         * Parallel mode only supports complete execution of a plan. "ExecutorStart(QueryDesc *queryDesc, int eflags)\n{\n        /*\n         * In some cases (e.g. an EXECUTE statement or an execute message with the\n         * extended query protocol) the query_id won't be reported, so do it now.\n         *\n         * Note that it's harmless to report the query_id multiple times, as the\n         * call will be ignored if the top level query_id has already been\n         * reported.\n         */\n        pgstat_report_query_id(queryDesc->plannedstmt->queryId, false);\n\n        if (ExecutorStart_hook)\n                (*ExecutorStart_hook) (queryDesc, eflags);\n        else\n                standard_ExecutorStart(queryDesc, eflags);\n}\n\nvoid\nstandard_ExecutorStart(QueryDesc *queryDesc, int eflags)\n{\n        EState     *estate;\n        MemoryContext oldcontext;\n\n        /* sanity checks: queryDesc must not be started already */\n        Assert(queryDesc != NULL);\n        Assert(queryDesc->estate == NULL);\n\n        /* caller must ensure the query's snapshot is active */\n        Assert(GetActiveSnapshot() == queryDesc->snapshot);\n\n        /*\n         * If the transaction is read-only, we need to check if any writes are\n         * planned to non-temporary tables.  EXPLAIN is considered read-only.\n         *\n         * Don't allow writes in parallel mode.  Supporting UPDATE and DELETE\n         * would require (a) storing the combo CID hash in shared memory, rather\n         * than synchronizing it just once at the start of parallelism, and (b) an\n         * alternative to heap_update()'s reliance on xmax for mutual exclusion.\n         * INSERT may have no such troubles, but we forbid it to simplify the\n         * checks.\n         *\n         * We have lower-level defenses in CommandCounterIncrement and elsewhere\n         * against performing unsafe operations in parallel mode, but this gives a\n         * more user-friendly error message.\n         */\n        if ((XactReadOnly || IsInParallelMode()) &&\n                !(eflags & EXEC_FLAG_EXPLAIN_ONLY))\n                ExecCheckXactReadOnly(queryDesc->plannedstmt);\n\n        /*\n         * Build EState, switch into per-query memory context for startup.\n         */\n        estate = CreateExecutorState();\n        queryDesc->estate = estate;\n\n        oldcontext = MemoryContextSwitchTo(estate->es_query_cxt);\n\n        /*\n         * Fill in external parameters, if any, from queryDesc; and allocate\n         * workspace for internal parameters\n         */\n        estate->es_param_list_info = queryDesc->params;\n\n        if (queryDesc->plannedstmt->paramExecTypes != NIL)\n        {\n                int                     nParamExec;\n\n                nParamExec = list_length(queryDesc->plannedstmt->paramExecTypes);\n                estate->es_param_exec_vals = (ParamExecData *)\n                        palloc0(nParamExec * sizeof(ParamExecData));\n        }\n\n        /* We now require all callers to provide sourceText */\n        Assert(queryDesc->sourceText != NULL);\n        estate->es_sourceText = queryDesc->sourceText;\n\n        /*\n         * Fill in the query environment, if any, from queryDesc.\n         */\n        estate->es_queryEnv = queryDesc->queryEnv;\n\n        /*\n         * If non-read-only query, set the command ID to mark output tuples with\n         */\n        switch (queryDesc->operation)\n        {\n                case CMD_SELECT:\n\n                        /*\n                         * SELECT FOR [KEY] UPDATE/SHARE and modifying CTEs need to mark\n                         * tuples\n                         */\n                        if (queryDesc->plannedstmt->rowMarks != NIL ||\n                                queryDesc->plannedstmt->hasModifyingCTE)\n                                estate->es_output_cid = GetCurrentCommandId(true);\n\n                        /*\n                         * A SELECT without modifying CTEs can't possibly queue triggers,\n                         * so force skip-triggers mode. This is just a marginal efficiency\n                         * hack, since AfterTriggerBeginQuery/AfterTriggerEndQuery aren't\n                         * all that expensive, but we might as well do it.\n                         */\n                        if (!queryDesc->plannedstmt->hasModifyingCTE)\n                                eflags |= EXEC_FLAG_SKIP_TRIGGERS;\n                        break;\n\n                case CMD_INSERT:\n                case CMD_DELETE:\n                case CMD_UPDATE:\n                case CMD_MERGE:\n                        estate->es_output_cid = GetCurrentCommandId(true);\n                        break;\n\n                default:\n                        elog(ERROR, \"unrecognized operation code: %d\",\n                                 (int) queryDesc->operation);\n                        break;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Copy other important information into the EState\n         */\n        estate->es_snapshot = RegisterSnapshot(queryDesc->snapshot);\n        estate->es_crosscheck_snapshot = RegisterSnapshot(queryDesc->crosscheck_snapshot);\n        estate->es_top_eflags = eflags;\n        estate->es_instrument = queryDesc->instrument_options;\n        estate->es_jit_flags = queryDesc->plannedstmt->jitFlags;\n\n        /*\n         * Set up an AFTER-trigger statement context, unless told not to, or\n         * unless it's EXPLAIN-only mode (when ExecutorFinish won't be called).\n         */\n        if (!(eflags & (EXEC_FLAG_SKIP_TRIGGERS | EXEC_FLAG_EXPLAIN_ONLY)))\n                AfterTriggerBeginQuery();\n\n        /*\n         * Initialize the plan state tree\n         */\n        InitPlan(queryDesc, eflags);\n\n        MemoryContextSwitchTo(oldcontext);\n}\n\n/* ----------------------------------------------------------------\n *              ExecutorRun\n *\n *              This is the main routine of the executor module. "* standard_planner().\n *\n * Note to plugin authors: standard_planner() scribbles on its Query input,\n * so you'd better copy that data structure if you want to plan more than once.\n *\n *****************************************************************************/\nPlannedStmt *\nplanner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,\n                ParamListInfo boundParams)\n{\n        PlannedStmt *result;\n\n        if (planner_hook)\n                result = (*planner_hook) (parse, query_string, cursorOptions, boundParams);\n        else\n                result = standard_planner(parse, query_string, cursorOptions, boundParams);\n\n        pgstat_report_plan_id(result->planId, false);\n\n        return result;\n}\n\nPlannedStmt *\nstandard_planner(Query *parse, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,\n                                 ParamListInfo boundParams)\n{\n        PlannedStmt *result;\n        PlannerGlobal *glob;\n        double          tuple_fraction;\n        PlannerInfo *root;\n        RelOptInfo *final_rel;\n        Path       *best_path;\n        Plan       *top_plan;\n        ListCell   *lp,\n                           *lr;\n\n        /*\n         * Set up global state for this planner invocation. We\n         * can't do this in a standalone backend, or if the command will try to\n         * modify any data, or if this is a cursor operation, or if GUCs are set\n         * to values that don't permit parallelism, or if parallel-unsafe\n         * functions are present in the query tree.\n         *\n         * (Note that we do allow CREATE TABLE AS, SELECT INTO, and CREATE\n         * MATERIALIZED VIEW to use parallel plans, but this is safe only because\n         * the command is writing into a completely new table which workers won't\n         * be able to see.  If the workers could see the table, the fact that\n         * group locking would cause them to ignore the leader's heavyweight GIN\n         * page locks would make this unsafe.  We'll have to fix that somehow if\n         * we want to allow parallel inserts in general; updates and deletes have\n         * additional problems especially around combo CIDs.)\n         *\n         * For now, we don't try to use parallel mode if we're running inside a\n         * parallel worker. It's not safe to do so if\n         * the query contains anything parallel-unsafe; parallelModeOK will be\n         * false in that case.  Note that parallelModeOK can't change after this\n         * point. Otherwise, everything in the query is either parallel-safe or\n         * parallel-restricted, and in either case it should be OK to impose\n         * parallel-mode restrictions. So\n                         * for now, bail out if we see a temporary table.\n                         */\n                        if (get_rel_persistence(rte->relid) == RELPERSISTENCE_TEMP)\n                                return;\n\n                        /*\n                         * Table sampling can be pushed down to workers if the sample\n                         * function and its arguments are safe.\n                         */\n                        if (rte->tablesample != NULL)\n                        {\n                                char            proparallel = func_parallel(rte->tablesample->tsmhandler);\n\n                                if (proparallel != PROPARALLEL_SAFE)\n                                        return;\n                                if (!is_parallel_safe(root, (Node *) rte->tablesample->args))\n                                        return;\n                        }\n\n                        /*\n                         * Ask FDWs whether they can support performing a ForeignScan\n                         * within a worker.  Most often, the answer will be no.  For\n                         * example, if the nature of the FDW is such that it opens a TCP\n                         * connection with a remote server, each parallel worker would end\n                         * up with a separate connection, and these connections might not\n                         * be appropriately coordinated between workers and the leader.\n                         */\n                        if (rte->relkind == RELKIND_FOREIGN_TABLE)\n                        {\n                                Assert(rel->fdwroutine);\n                                if (!rel->fdwroutine->IsForeignScanParallelSafe)\n                                        return;\n                                if (!rel->fdwroutine->IsForeignScanParallelSafe(root, rel, rte))\n                                        return;\n                        }\n\n                        /*\n                         * There are additional considerations for appendrels, which we'll\n                         * deal with in set_append_rel_size and set_append_rel_pathlist.\n                         * For now, just set consider_parallel based on the rel's own\n                         * quals and targetlist.\n                         */\n                        break;\n\n                case RTE_SUBQUERY:\n\n                        /*\n                         * There's no intrinsic problem with scanning a subquery-in-FROM\n                         * (as distinct from a SubPlan or InitPlan) in a parallel worker.\n                         * If the subquery doesn't happen to have any parallel-safe paths,\n                         * then flagging it as consider_parallel won't change anything,\n                         * but that's true for plain tables, too.  We must set\n                         * consider_parallel based on the rel's own quals and targetlist,\n                         * so that if a subquery path is parallel-safe but the quals and\n                         * projection we're sticking onto it are not, we correctly mark\n                         * the SubqueryScanPath as not parallel-safe.  (Note that\n                         * set_subquery_pathlist() might push some of these quals down\n                         * into the subquery itself, but that doesn't change anything.)\n                         *\n                         * We can't push sub-select containing LIMIT/OFFSET to workers as\n                         * there is no guarantee that the row order will be fully\n                         * deterministic, and applying LIMIT/OFFSET will lead to\n                         * inconsistent results at the top-level.  (In some cases, where\n                         * the result is ordered, we could relax this restriction.  But it\n                         * doesn't currently seem worth expending extra effort to do so.)\n                         */\n                        {\n                                Query      *subquery = castNode(Query, rte->subquery);\n\n                                if (limit_needed(subquery))\n                                        return;\n                        }\n                        break;\n\n                case RTE_JOIN:\n                        /* Shouldn't happen; we're only considering baserels here. */\n                        Assert(false);\n                        return;\n\n                case RTE_FUNCTION:\n                        /* Check for parallel-restricted functions. */\n                        if (!is_parallel_safe(root, (Node *) rte->functions))\n                                return;\n                        break;\n\n                case RTE_TABLEFUNC:\n                        /* not parallel safe */\n                        return;\n\n                case RTE_VALUES:\n                        /* Check for parallel-restricted functions. */\n                        if (!is_parallel_safe(root, (Node *) rte->values_lists))\n                                return;\n                        break;\n\n                case RTE_CTE:\n\n                        /*\n                         * CTE tuplestores aren't shared among parallel workers, so we\n                         * force all CTE scans to happen in the leader.  Also, populating\n                         * the CTE would require executing a subplan that's not available\n                         * in the worker, might be parallel-restricted, and must get\n                         * executed only once.\n                         */\n                        return;\n\n                case RTE_NAMEDTUPLESTORE:\n\n                        /*\n                         * tuplestore cannot be shared, at least without more\n                         * infrastructure to support that.\n                         */\n                        return;\n\n                case RTE_RESULT:\n                        /* RESULT RTEs, in themselves, are no problem. */\n                        break;\n                case RTE_GROUP:\n                        /* Shouldn't happen; we're only considering baserels here. */\n                        Assert(false);\n                        return;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * If there's anything in baserestrictinfo that's parallel-restricted, we\n         * give up on parallelizing access to this relation.  We could consider\n         * instead postponing application of the restricted quals until we're\n         * above all the parallelism in the plan tree, but it's not clear that\n         * that would be a win in very many cases, and it might be tricky to make\n         * outer join clauses work correctly.  It would likely break equivalence\n         * classes, too.\n         */\n        if (!is_parallel_safe(root, (Node *) rel->baserestrictinfo))\n                return;\n\n        /*\n         * Likewise, if the relation's outputs are not parallel-safe, give up.\n         * (Usually, they're just Vars, but sometimes they're not.)\n         */\n        if (!is_parallel_safe(root, (Node *) rel->reltarget->exprs))\n                return;\n\n        /* We have a winner. */\n        rel->consider_parallel = true;\n}\n\n/*\n * set_plain_rel_pathlist\n *        Build access paths for a plain relation (no subquery, no inheritance)\n */\nstatic void\nset_plain_rel_pathlist(PlannerInfo *root, RelOptInfo *rel, RangeTblEntry *rte)\n{\n        Relids          required_outer;\n\n        /*\n         * We don't support pushing join clauses into the quals of a seqscan, but\n         * it could still have required parameterization due to LATERAL refs in\n         * its tlist.\n         */\n        required_outer = rel->lateral_relids;\n\n        /*\n         * Consider TID scans.\n         *\n         * If create_tidscan_paths returns true, then a TID scan path is forced.\n         * This happens when rel->baserestrictinfo contains CurrentOfExpr, because\n         * the executor can't handle any other type of path for such queries.\n         * Hence, we return without adding any other paths."

"* the result of joining all the original relations together.\n * At least one implementation path must be provided for this relation and\n * all required sub-relations.\n *\n * To support loadable plugins that modify planner behavior by changing the\n * join searching algorithm, we provide a hook variable that lets a plugin\n * replace or supplement this function.  Any such hook must return the same\n * final join relation as the standard code would, but it might have a\n * different set of implementation paths attached, and only the sub-joinrels\n * needed for these paths need have been instantiated.\n *\n * Note to plugin authors: the functions invoked during standard_join_search()\n * modify root->join_rel_list and root->join_rel_hash.  If you want to do more\n * than one join-order search, you'll probably need to save and restore the\n * original states of those data structures.  See geqo_eval() for an example.\n */\nRelOptInfo *\nstandard_join_search(PlannerInfo *root, int levels_needed, List *initial_rels)\n{\n        int                     lev;\n        RelOptInfo *rel;\n\n        /*\n         * This function cannot be invoked recursively within any one planning\n         * problem, so join_rel_level[] can't be in use already.\n         */\n        Assert(root->join_rel_level == NULL);\n\n        /*\n         * We employ a simple \"dynamic programming\" algorithm: we first find all\n         * ways to build joins of two jointree items, then all ways to build joins\n         * of three items (from two-item joins and single items), then four-item\n         * joins, and so on until we have considered all ways to join all the\n         * items into one rel.\n         *\n         * root->join_rel_level[j] is a list of all the j-item rels.  Initially we\n         * set root->join_rel_level[1] to represent all the single-jointree-item\n         * relations.\n         */\n        root->join_rel_level = (List **) palloc0((levels_needed + 1) * sizeof(List *));\n\n        root->join_rel_level[1] = initial_rels;\n\n        for (lev = 2; lev <= levels_needed; lev++)\n        {\n                ListCell   *lc;\n\n                /*\n                 * Determine all possible pairs of relations to be joined at this\n                 * level, and build paths for making each one from every available\n                 * pair of lower-level relations.\n                 */\n                join_search_one_level(root, lev);\n\n                /*\n                 * Run generate_partitionwise_join_paths() and\n                 * generate_useful_gather_paths() for each just-processed joinrel.  We\n                 * could not do this earlier because both regular and partial paths\n                 * can get added to a particular joinrel at multiple times within\n                 * join_search_one_level.\n                 *\n                 * After that, we're done creating paths for the joinrel, so run\n                 * set_cheapest().\n                 */\n                foreach(lc, root->join_rel_level[lev])\n                {\n                        rel = (RelOptInfo *) lfirst(lc);\n\n                        /* Create paths for partitionwise joins. */\n                        generate_partitionwise_join_paths(root, rel);\n\n                        /*\n                         * Except for the topmost scan/join rel, consider gathering\n                         * partial paths.  We'll do the same for the topmost scan/join rel\n                         * once we know the final targetlist (see grouping_planner's and\n                         * its call to apply_scanjoin_target_to_paths).\n                         */\n                        if (!bms_equal(rel->relids, root->all_query_rels))\n                                generate_useful_gather_paths(root, rel, false);\n\n                        /* Find and save the cheapest paths for this rel */\n                        set_cheapest(rel);\n\n#ifdef OPTIMIZER_DEBUG\n                        pprint(rel);\n#endif\n                }\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * We should have a single rel at the final level.\n         */\n        if (root->join_rel_level[levels_needed] == NIL)\n                elog(ERROR, \"failed to build any %d-way joins\", levels_needed);\n        Assert(list_length(root->join_rel_level[levels_needed]) == 1);\n\n        rel = (RelOptInfo *) linitial(root->join_rel_level[levels_needed]);\n\n        root->join_rel_level = NULL;\n\n        return rel;\n}\n\n/*****************************************************************************\n *                      PUSHING QUALS DOWN INTO SUBQUERIES\n *****************************************************************************/\n\n/*\n * subquery_is_pushdown_safe - is a subquery safe for pushing down quals?\n *\n * subquery is the particular component query being checked.  topquery\n * is the top component of a set-operations tree (the same Query if no\n * set-op is involved).\n *\n * Conditions checked here:\n *\n * 1. If the subquery has a LIMIT clause, we must not push down any quals,\n * since that could change the set of rows returned.\n *\n * 2. If the subquery contains EXCEPT or EXCEPT ALL set ops we cannot push\n * quals into it, because that could change the results."

A `DO INSTEAD` rule can replace the original query with zero or many new queries. Rules may expand one query into several (e.g., an `INSERT` on a view becomes `INSERT` + `UPDATE` on base tables).\n- **`fireRIRrules()`** applies rules for relations being read (RIR = Rule Is Read). Programming\n\n**File:** `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c`, line 3457.\n\n```c\nfor (lev = 2; lev <= levels_needed; lev++)\n{\n    join_search_one_level(root, lev);   /* build all lev-way join  /* keep cheapest_total_path, cheapest_startup_path */\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAt level 2, every pair of base relations is tried. At level 3, every pair of a level-2 joinrel and a base rel is tried, and so on. `join_search_one_level()` considers both left-deep and bushy join trees; for each candidate pair it calls `make_join_rel()`, which enumerates NestLoop, MergeJoin, and HashJoin paths through `try_nestloop_path()`, `try_mergejoin_path()`, and `try_hashjoin_path()`, ultimately calling `add_path()`.\n\n#### The `Path` Struct\n\n**File:** `src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h`, line 1753.\n\n```c\ntypedef struct Path {\n    NodeTag         pathtype;          /* T_SeqScan, T_IndexScan, T_HashJoin, \u2026 */\n    RelOptInfo     *parent;            /* the relation this path is for */\n    PathTarget     *pathtarget;        /* output expression list + cost */\n    ParamPathInfo  *param_info;        /* parameterization info (NestLoop inner) */\n    bool            parallel_aware;\n    bool            parallel_safe;\n    int             parallel_workers;\n    Cardinality     rows;              /* estimated output row count */\n    int             disabled_nodes;   /* count of nodes disabled by enable_xxx GUCs */\n    Cost            startup_cost;      /* cost before first tuple */\n    Cost            total_cost;        /* total cost */\n    List           *pathkeys;          /* sort ordering of output */\n} Path;\n```\n\nSpecialised subtypes (`IndexPath`, `JoinPath`, `HashPath`, etc.) extend this header with type-specific fields.\n\n#### The `RelOptInfo` Struct\n\n**File:** `src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h`, line 883.\n\nA `RelOptInfo` represents either a base relation or a join of several relations. Key fields:\n\n| Field | Description |\n|-------|-------------|\n| `relids` | Bitmapset of base-rel RT indexes in this join |\n| `rows` | Estimated output cardinality |\n| `pathlist` | All complete `Path`s for this rel |\n| `partial_pathlist` | Parallel-worker partial paths |\n| `cheapest_startup_path` | Best path for fast first tuple |\n| `cheapest_total_path` | Best path for full result |\n| `pages`, `tuples` | Physical size from `pg_class` |\n| `baserestrictinfo` | Restriction clauses (WHERE conditions) |\n| `joininfo` | Join clauses referencing other rels |\n| `indexlist` | Available `IndexOptInfo`s |\n\n### `create_plan()` \u2014 Path \u2192 Plan Tree\n\n**File:** `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c`, line 337.\n\n`create_plan()` calls `create_plan_recurse()`, which dispatches on `best_path->pathtype`:\n\n```\ncreate_plan_recurse()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_SeqScan / T_IndexScan / T_IndexOnlyScan / T_BitmapHeapScan / \u2026\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 create_scan_plan()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_NestLoop / T_MergeJoin / T_HashJoin\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 create_join_plan()      (recurses into inner/outer subpaths)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_Append / T_MergeAppend      \u2192 create_append_plan()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_Agg / T_Group / T_WindowAgg \u2192 create_agg_plan() / \u2026\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_Sort / T_IncrementalSort    \u2192 create_sort_plan()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_Limit                       \u2192 create_limit_plan()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_Gather / T_GatherMerge      \u2192 create_gather_plan() / \u2026\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 T_ModifyTable                 \u2192 create_modifytable_plan()\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 \u2026 (all plan node types)\n```\n\nEach `create_xxx_plan()` function allocates a typed `Plan` node, copies cost estimates and the target list from the `Path`, and recursively builds child plan nodes. The result is a `Plan` tree.\n\n### Output: `PlannedStmt`\n\n**File:** `src/include/nodes/plannodes.h`, line 46.\n\n```c\ntypedef struct PlannedStmt {\n    CmdType      commandType;       /* SELECT / INSERT / UPDATE / \u2026 */\n    int64        queryId;\n    int64        planId;\n    bool         hasReturning;\n    bool         hasModifyingCTE;\n    bool         canSetTag;\n    bool         parallelModeNeeded;\n    int          jitFlags;          /* PGJIT_PERFORM | PGJIT_EXPR | \u2026 */\n    struct Plan *planTree;          /* root Plan node */\n    List        *rtable;            /* final range table */\n    List        *permInfos;         /* RTEPermissionInfo entries */\n    List        *resultRelations;   /* target rel RT indexes */\n    List        *subplans;          /* SubPlan / InitPlan trees */\n    List        *rowMarks;          /* FOR UPDATE / SHARE marks */\n    List        *relationOids;      /* OIDs for plan invalidation */\n    List        *invalItems;        /* other invalidation dependencies */\n    List        *paramExecTypes;    /* types of PARAM_EXEC slots */\n    ...\n} PlannedStmt;\n```\n\n---\n\n## Stage 5 \u2014 Portal Management\n\n**File:** `src/backend/tcop/pquery.c`.\n\nThe `Portal` abstraction decouples query preparation from execution and supports cursors and partial fetches.\n\n### `PortalDefineQuery()`\n\nStores the `List<PlannedStmt>`, the original source text, and the command tag in the portal.\n\n### `PortalStart()` (line 434)\n\nDetermines the portal strategy via `ChoosePortalStrategy()`:\n\n| Strategy | Condition | Action |\n|----------|-----------|--------|\n| `PORTAL_ONE_SELECT` | Single `SELECT` | `CreateQueryDesc()` + `ExecutorStart()` immediately |\n| `PORTAL_ONE_RETURNING` | DML with `RETURNING` | Defers `ExecutorStart()` until `PortalRun()` |\n| `PORTAL_ONE_MOD_WITH` | Modifying CTE | Same deferred pattern |\n| `PORTAL_UTIL_SELECT` | Utility that returns tuples | Sets `tupDesc` only |\n| `PORTAL_MULTI_QUERY` | Multiple or mixed stmts | No-op; handled per-stmt in `PortalRunMulti()` |\n\nFor `PORTAL_ONE_SELECT`:\n```c\nqueryDesc = CreateQueryDesc(plannedstmt, sourceText, snapshot, ...);\nExecutorStart(queryDesc, myeflags);\nportal->queryDesc = queryDesc;\nportal->tupDesc   = queryDesc->tupDesc;\n```\n\n`CreateQueryDesc()` bundles the `PlannedStmt`, snapshot, `DestReceiver`, and parameter bindings into a `QueryDesc` \u2014 the package handed to every executor entry point.\n\n### `PortalRun()` (line 685)\n\nRoutes execution by strategy:\n- `PORTAL_ONE_SELECT` \u2192 **`PortalRunSelect()`** \u2192 `ExecutorRun()`\n- `PORTAL_ONE_RETURNING` / `PORTAL_ONE_MOD_WITH` \u2192 **`PortalRunMulti()`** \u2192 `ProcessQuery()` \u2192 `ExecutorStart()` + `ExecutorRun()`\n- `PORTAL_UTIL_SELECT` \u2192 **`PortalRunUtility()`** \u2192 `ProcessUtility()`\n- `PORTAL_MULTI_QUERY` \u2192 **`PortalRunMulti()`** \u2014 iterates statements\n\n---\n\n## Stage 6 \u2014 Executor\n\n**Files:** `src/backend/executor/execMain.c`, `src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c`.\n\n### `ExecutorStart()` \u2192 `standard_ExecutorStart()` (line 141)\n\n1. Calls `pgstat_report_query_id()`.\n2. Allocates an `EState` via `CreateExecutorState()` \u2014 the per-execution state object.\n3. Populates `EState` from `QueryDesc`: snapshot, parameter values, source text, query environment, command ID, JIT flags.\n4. Calls `AfterTriggerBeginQuery()` unless triggers are skipped.\n5. Calls **`InitPlan()`**.\n\n#### `InitPlan()` (line 836)\n\n1. `ExecCheckPermissions()` \u2014 verifies ACLs for all range table entries.\n2. `ExecInitRangeTable()` \u2014 opens relations, acquires locks.\n3. `ExecDoInitialPruning()` \u2014 prunes partition children that cannot satisfy constraints.\n4. Iterates `plannedstmt->subplans`, calling `ExecInitNode()` for each SubPlan / InitPlan.\n5. Calls **`ExecInitNode(plan, estate, eflags)`** on the root plan node \u2014 this builds the entire `PlanState` tree.\n6. Sets `queryDesc->tupDesc` and `queryDesc->planstate`.\n\n#### `ExecInitNode()` (line 142 in `execProcnode.c`)\n\nRecursively mirrors the `Plan` tree to build a `PlanState` tree:\n\n```c\nswitch (nodeTag(node))\n{\n    case T_SeqScan:       return ExecInitSeqScan(...);\n    case T_IndexScan:     return ExecInitIndexScan(...);\n    case T_IndexOnlyScan: return ExecInitIndexOnlyScan(...);\n    case T_BitmapHeapScan:return ExecInitBitmapHeapScan(...);\n    case T_NestLoop:      return ExecInitNestLoop(...);\n    case T_MergeJoin:     return ExecInitMergeJoin(...);\n    case T_HashJoin:      return ExecInitHashJoin(...);\n    case T_Agg:           return ExecInitAgg(...);\n    case T_Sort:          return ExecInitSort(...);\n    case T_Limit:         return ExecInitLimit(...);\n    case T_ModifyTable:   return ExecInitModifyTable(...);\n    case T_Gather:        return ExecInitGather(...);\n    /* \u2026 all node types \u2026 */\n}\n```\n\nAfter `ExecInitNode()` returns, `ExecSetExecProcNode()` installs an `ExecProcNodeFirst` wrapper that checks stack depth on the first call and optionally wraps with `ExecProcNodeInstr` for instrumentation.\n\n### The `PlanState` Struct\n\n**File:** `src/include/nodes/execnodes.h`, line 1149.\n\n```c\ntypedef struct PlanState {\n    NodeTag            type;\n    Plan              *plan;               /* corresponding Plan node */\n    EState            *state;              /* shared EState for this query */\n    ExecProcNodeMtd    ExecProcNode;       /* function pointer: returns next tuple */\n    ExecProcNodeMtd    ExecProcNodeReal;   /* actual function (unwrapped) */\n    Instrumentation   *instrument;         /* runtime stats (EXPLAIN ANALYZE) */\n    ExprState         *qual;               /* boolean qual condition */\n    struct PlanState  *lefttree;           /* left child */\n    struct PlanState  *righttree;          /* right child */\n    List              *initPlan;           /* InitPlan SubPlanState nodes */\n    List              *subPlan;            /* correlated SubPlanState nodes */\n    Bitmapset         *chgParam;           /* changed parameters (for rescan) */\n    TupleDesc          ps_ResultTupleDesc;\n    TupleTableSlot    *ps_ResultTupleSlot;\n    ExprContext       *ps_ExprContext;\n    ProjectionInfo    *ps_ProjInfo;\n    bool               async_capable;\n} PlanState;\n```\n\nEvery concrete executor node (e.g., `SeqScanState`, `HashJoinState`) embeds `PlanState` as its first member, enabling safe casting.\n\n### The `EState` Struct\n\n**File:** `src/include/nodes/execnodes.h`, line 649.\n\nThe `EState` is the per-query execution state shared by all nodes in the plan tree. Notable fields:\n\n| Field | Description |\n|-------|-------------|\n| `es_direction` | `ForwardScanDirection` / `BackwardScanDirection` |\n| `es_snapshot` | MVCC snapshot for visibility checks |\n| `es_range_table` | Range table (list of `RangeTblEntry`) |\n| `es_relations` | Array of open `Relation` handles per RT entry |\n| `es_plannedstmt` | Pointer back to the `PlannedStmt` |\n| `es_output_cid` | Command ID for marking new tuples (DML) |\n| `es_result_relations` | `ResultRelInfo` array for INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE targets |\n| `es_param_list_info` | External parameter values |\n| `es_param_exec_vals` | Internal `PARAM_EXEC` (subplan) values |\n| `es_query_cxt` | Per-query memory context |\n| `es_tupleTable` | List of all `TupleTableSlot`s |\n| `es_processed` | Tuples processed in current `ExecutorRun()` call |\n| `es_total_processed` | Cumulative tuples across all calls (cursor fetch) |\n| `es_instrument` | Instrumentation flags (`INSTRUMENT_TIMER`, etc.) |\n| `es_use_parallel_mode` | Whether workers were launched |\n| `es_jit` | JIT context (if `jitFlags` non-zero) |\n\n### `ExecutorRun()` \u2192 `standard_ExecutorRun()` \u2192 `ExecutePlan()` (line 307 / 1660)\n\n```c\nvoid standard_ExecutorRun(QueryDesc *queryDesc, ScanDirection direction, uint64 count)\n{\n    sendTuples = (operation == CMD_SELECT || plannedstmt->hasReturning);\n    if (sendTuples)\n        dest->rStartup(dest, operation, queryDesc->tupDesc);\n\n    ExecutePlan(queryDesc, operation, sendTuples, count, direction, dest);\n\n    estate->es_total_processed += estate->es_processed;\n    if (sendTuples)\n        dest->rShutdown(dest);\n}\n```\n\n`ExecutePlan()` is the core Volcano pull-model loop:\n\n```c\nfor (;;)\n{\n    ResetPerTupleExprContext(estate);          /* free per-output-tuple memory */\n    slot = ExecProcNode(planstate);            /* pull next tuple */\n    if (TupIsNull(slot)) break;\n\n    if (estate->es_junkFilter)\n        slot = ExecFilterJunk(estate->es_junkFilter, slot);\n\n    if (sendTuples)\n        if (!dest->receiveSlot(slot, dest)) break;  /* send to client */\n\n    if (operation == CMD_SELECT)\n        estate->es_processed++;\n\n    if (numberTuples && numberTuples == ++current_tuple_count) break;\n}\n```\n\n### Volcano Pull Model\n\nEvery `PlanState` node implements `ExecProcNode` as a function pointer returning one `TupleTableSlot *` per call (or `NULL` at end-of-stream). Parent nodes call `ExecProcNode(child)` to pull tuples from their children:\n\n```\nExecProcNode(LimitState)\n  \u2514\u2500\u25ba ExecProcNode(SortState)\n        \u2514\u2500\u25ba ExecProcNode(HashJoinState)\n              \u251c\u2500\u25ba ExecProcNode(SeqScanState)   \u2190 outer relation\n              \u2514\u2500\u25ba MultiExecProcNode(HashState) \u2190 builds hash table from inner\n                    \u2514\u2500\u25ba ExecProcNode(IndexScanState)\n```\n\n- **`ExecProcNodeFirst()`** \u2014 one-time wrapper: checks stack depth, then swaps itself out for `ExecProcNodeReal` (or `ExecProcNodeInstr` if instrumentation is on).\n- **`ExecProcNodeInstr()`** \u2014 wraps each call with `InstrStartNode()` / `InstrStopNode()` for `EXPLAIN ANALYZE` timing.\n- **`MultiExecProcNode()`** \u2014 used for nodes that produce a bulk data structure (e.g., `Hash` building a hash table, `BitmapIndexScan` building a bitmap) rather than individual tuples.\n\n### `DestReceiver`\n\nThe `DestReceiver` interface (`dest->receiveSlot()`, `dest->rStartup()`, `dest->rShutdown()`, `dest->rDestroy()`) abstracts tuple delivery:\n\n| Destination | Usage |\n|-------------|-------|\n| `DestRemote` | Wire-format rows sent to the client via `libpq` |\n| `DestNone` | Discard tuples (MOVE cursor, some internal paths) |\n| `DestCopyOut` | COPY TO target |\n| `DestIntoRel` | CREATE TABLE AS / SELECT INTO |\n| `DestTransientRel` | Materialized CTEs, REFRESH MATERIALIZED VIEW |\n| `DestSQLFunction` | Tuples consumed inside SQL-language functions |\n\n---\n\n## End-to-End Data Flow
